1,5,"Program number which is used for parameter compatibility check.||Normally same value than MAND.PRGNR||||If a firmware variant should be parameter compatible to a standard firmware, the variant must return the program number of the standard firmware here.||||Example:||Standard firmware of LXM32M = PR912.00||OEM firmware PR912.10 which should be parameter compatible must return 91200 in this value (not 91210).||Component: ADM||"
"TIP"
1,6,"Current parameter version number (belongs to MAND.CFGPRGNR)||Has normally the same value than MAND.VERSION.||||This value is stored in a parameter configuration.||A configuration can only be loaded in a drive which has a value equal or greater.||||If a firmware version is increased, but is forward AND backward compatible, then this value should NOT be increased. ||This would allow to download a new configuration in an old drive.||Component: ADM||"

1,28,"Read : Message||Write: Confirm or Cancel Start-up/Cyclic Message bits, see bit 31||||Read:||Bit 0 = 1: 'First Setup'||Bit 1 = 1: Motor changed||Bit 2 = 1: Eeprom data corrupted||Bit 3 = 1: No motor connected||Bit 4 = 1: Change of a parameter which is activated after restart||Bit 5 = 1: Memory card changed/detected with modified data (different S/N and/or write counter) ||Bit 6 = 1: Unknown Memory card detected (unknown data structure)||Bit 7 = 1: Invalid configuration (see parameter STD.INVALIDPARAM)||Bit 8 = 1: Memory card removed (Fast device replacement (FDR) no more possible).||Bit 9 = 1: Module in Slot1 removed||Bit 10 = 1: Module in Slot2 removed or changed||Bit 11 = 1: Module in Slot3 removed or changed||Bit 12 = 1: Memory card with wrong format or file size detected||Bit 13 ... 30: reserved||||Write:||Bit 31: 0=Confirm, 1=Cancel (additional bit)||||Bit 0 = 1: Confirm 'First Setup' (implicit done, not possible by user)||Bit 1 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Motor changed'||Bit 2 ... 3: reserved||Bit 4 = 1: Confirm 'Change of a startup parameter'||Bit 5 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Memory card changed'||Bit 6 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'unknown Memory card detected'||Bit 7 = 1: 'Invalid configuration' (no action possible)||Bit 8 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Memory card removed'||Bit 9 = 1: Confirm 'Module in Slot1 removed'||Bit 10 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Module in Slot2 removed or changed'||Bit 11 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Module in Slot3 removed or changed'||Bit 12 = 1: Confirm/Cancel 'Memory card with wrong format or file size detected'||Bit 13 ... 30: reserved||||Availability of bits depends on product.||Komponente : PMS||||Wurth, 26.02.2007:||Parameter nicht mehr in Doku, da nur für HMI+Inbetriebnahmetool verwendet. ||Beschreibung für Anwender siehe Doku Kapitel 'Service / Changing the motor'||"

4,9,"This parameter allows file transfer with usage of ordinary 32bit parameters.||||1. Write access defines the file to transfer and initializes the transfer.||  The file is defined with UMAS like file identification:||  Highword Highbyte = id1||  Highword Lowbyte = id2||  Lowword Highbyte = id3||  Lowword Lowbyte = id4||  For comaptibility issues, the special id 0x00170032 is treated as FastScope data file.||||2. "TIP"
4,10,"This parameter allows file download with usage of ordinary 32bit parameters:||||1. Write access defines the file to transfer and initializes the transfer.||  The file is defined with UMAS like file identification:||  Highword Highbyte = id1||  Highword Lowbyte = id2||  Lowword Highbyte = id3||  Lowword Lowbyte = id4||||2. In parameter BLOCKLENGTH the file length in words has to be written.||  This value is automatically decremented by the drive during the transfer.||||3. By repeated writing of parameter BLOCKDATA the data is transferred in 32bit packages.||||4. When the data is completely transmitted, parameter BLOCKLENGTH shows the value 0.||Komponente :||"
"TIP"
4,11,"For file upload: reading shows file length in words||For file download: writing defines file length in words||Komponente :||"
"TIP"
4,12,"see also PARAM.BLOCKUPINIT||||Each read/write access transfers two 16bit values, to be interpreted in the order high-word, low-word.||If an odd number of words is transmitted, the low-word of the last transmitted value is not relevant.||After the whole file is tranferred, additional access to this parameter results in an error response.||If the block transfer is not initialized, read access to this parameter returns the value 0, in order to pass the CANopen conformance test.||Komponente :||"

specifies the way position values are handled over a power cycle and allows for the simulation of an absolute position encoder using singleturn encoders.||||If this function is activated, the device saves the pertinent position data prior to a shutdown so that it can restore the mechanical position the next time it is switched on.||||In the case of singleturn encoders, the position can be restored if the motor shaft has not been moved by more than 0.25 revolutions while the drive was off.||||In the case of multiturn encoders, the permissible shaft movement while the drive is off can be much greater, depending on the type of multiturn encoder.||||For this function to work, the drive may only be shut down while the motor is at a standstill and the motor shaft must not be moved outside "TIP"
5,47,"A signal at the PTI interface is only evaluated if it is available for a time that is longer than the set filter time.||For example, if an interference pulse is available for a period shorter than the set filter time, the interference pulse is not evaluated.||||The interval between 2 signals must also be greater than the set filter time.||||Available with hardware version >=RS03.||Parameter für das digitale Hardware Filter am PTI Pulse Eingang.||Mit diesem Parameter wird die Dauer der Filterzeit festgelegt. D.h. der zeitliche Abstand zwischen 2 Flanken des Nutzsignals, welche einen Zählvorgang auslösen, muss länger sein, als diese parametrierte Zeit. Tritt eine Pulsflanke mit  einem kürzeren Zeitabstand zur letzten gezählten Flanke auf, so wird diese ausgefiltert und führt nicht zu einem Weiterzählen des Pulszählers. ||Besonderes Augenmerk muss auf die Bedeutung der Definition 'Flanken, die einen ordnungsgemäßen Zählvorgang auslösen, gelegt werden'. Hier gibt es deutliche Unterschiede zwischen den 3 möglichen Signalformen: A/B, P/R, und CW/CCW.||A/B-Signale: jede Flanke, egal ob steigend oder fallend, bewirkt einen Zählvorgang. Insofern muss bei dieser Signalform die Filterzeit wesentlich kleiner eingestellt werden, als der kleinstmögliche Abstand einer steigenden-A-Flanke zu einer steigenden B-Flanke bei einer ordnungsgemäßen, d.h. störungsfreien, Signalfolge.||P/R-Signale: hier bewirkt nur die steigende Puls-Flanke (P-Signal) einen Zählvorgang, ganz egal wie das Verhältnis Pulsdauer zu Pulspause ist. Bei dieser Signalform muss die Filterzeit deutlich kleiner eingestellt werden, als der kürzestmögliche Abstand zweier positiver Pulsflanken.||Gegebenenfalls vorhandene Toleranzen, Unsysmmetrien etc., die eine Verzögerung der Signale mit sich bringen, sind vom Anwender selbst einzurechnen bei der Parametriereung der Filterzeit. Mit anderen Worten: ist der Abstand zweier Zählflanken nur minimal kleiner als die parametrierte Filterzeit, so wird der letzte Puls ausgefiltert, d.h. nicht gezählt. ||Der default-Wert von 0,25µsec ist so klein gewählt, dass auch die maximal erlaubte Pulsfrequenz am PTI-Eingang problemlos gezählt werden kann. ||Dieses Filter ist nur auf der neuen LXM32 Hardware, welche mit einem neuen ASIC ausgestattet ist, vorhanden und wirksam. Auf älteren HW-Platformen ohne ASIC hat dieses Filter keine Bewandnis.||Einheit: µs mit 2 Nachkommastellen||Defaultwert: 25||"

25,1,"This parameter contains the control word in the MDT. It can be used for diagnostics purposes.||See [NT]SERCOS II V02.02[/NT] specifications for details.||||Bit 0: Service transport handshake of the master||||Bit 1: Service INFO||0: Read service INFO||1: Write service INFO||||Bit 2: Transmission||0: Transmission in progress||1: Last transmission||||Bits 3 ... 5: Data block element||0: Service channel not active, close service channel or break active transmission||1: IDN of the operation data. Service channel is closed for the previous IDN and opened for a new IDN||2: Name of operation data||3: Attribute of operation data||4: Unit of the operation data||5: Minimum input value||6: Maximum input value||7: Operation data||||Bit 6: Real-time control bit 1||||Bit 7: Real-time control bit 2||||Bit 8: Operating mode||0: Primary operating mode (IDN32)||1: Secondary operating mode (IDN33)||||Bits 9 ... 12: Reserved||||Bit 13: Halt/Restart (only possible if bits 14 and 15 are set to 1)||0: When the 'Halt/Restart' bit changes from 1 to 0, the drive decelerates with the HALT ramp.||1: When the 'Halt/Restart' bit changes from 0 to 1, the drive clears the HALT and follows the reference values of the master.||||Bit 14: Enable Drive||0: When the 'Enable Drive' bit changes from 1 to 0, the power stage is disabled.||1: When the 'Enable Drive' bit changes from 0 to 1, the power stage is enabled.||||Bit 15: Drive ON/OFF||0: When the 'Drive ON/OFF' bit changes from 1 to 0, the drive decelerates at the Quick Stop deceleration ramp. The power stage is disabled when a standstill is reached (error class 1).||1: When the 'Drive ON/OFF' bit changes from 0 to 1, the drive transitions to the operating state Operation Enabled (only possible if bits 13 and 14 are set to 1).||Komponente:||"

25,2,"This parameter contains the status word of the AT telegram. It can be used for diagnostics purposes.||See [NT]SERCOS II V02.02[/NT] specifications for details.||||Bit 0: Service transport handshake of the drive ||||Bit 1: Busy||0: Step finished, ready for new step||1: Step in progress, new step not permitted ||||Bit 2: Error in service channel||0: No error||1: Error in service channel, error message in drive service INFO||||Bit 3: Status of reference value processing||0: Drive ignores the reference values (e.g. during HALT)||1: Drive follows the reference values||||Bit 4: Reserved||||Bit 5: Change bit for procedure command||0: No change in procedure command||1: Change in procedure command||||Bit 6: Real-time status bit 1 (IDN304)||||Bit 7: Real-time status bit 2 (IDN306)||||Bit 8: Operating mode||0: Primary operating mode (IDN32)||1: Secondary operating mode (IDN33)||||Bits 9 ... 10: Reserved||||Bit 11: Change bit for C3D (IDN13)||0: No change||1: Change||||Bit 12: Change bit for C2D (IDN12)||0: No change||1: Change||||Bit 13: Error in C1D (IDN11)||0: No error||1: Error||||Bits 14 ... 15: Operating state||0: Drive not ready, internal checks not yet finished successfully (operating state: Not Ready To Switch On)||1: Drive ready for mains power on (operating state: Switch On Disabled)||2: Drive is ready, power stage is disabled (operating state: Ready To Switch On)||3: Drive operates, power stage is enabled (operating state: Operation Enabled).||Komponente:||"

27,5,"Velocity scaling may lead to values that cannot be represented as 16 bit values. 80,6,"Digital encoders:||Specification of the encoder increments the external encoder returns for one or several revolutions of the motor shaft.||The value is indicated with a numerator and a denominator so that it is possible, for example, to consider the gear ratio of a mechanical gearing. ||NOTE: The value may not be set to 0.||||The resolution factor is not applied until this numerator value is specified.||||Example: One motor revolution causes 1/3 encoder revolution at an encoder resolution of 16384 EncInc/revolution.||||ResolENC2Num         16384 EncInc||--------------------------- = -----------------------||ResolENC2Denom      3 revolutions||||||Analog encoders:||Num/Denom must be set equivalent to the number of analog periods per 1 motor revolution.||||Example: One motor revolution causes 1/3 encoder revolution at an encoder resolution of 16 analog periods per revolution.||||ResolENC2Num         16 periods||--------------------------- = --------------------||ResolENC2Denom      3 revolutions||Einheit: EncInc||Defaultwert: 10000||"

"TIP"
82,5,"Prgnr: 0000.00||This parameter is only relevant for SSI encoders (singleturn and multiturn). ||The maximum possible SSI transfer frequency is encoder-specific (specified by encoder manufacturer). The value of ENCDigSSIMaxFreq and the possible SSI transfer frequencies of the encoder module are used to configure an optimum SSI transfer frequency (the encoder module supports 0.2 MHz and 1 MHz transfer frequencies).||Example: The encoder has a maximum transfer frequency of 400 kHz. ENCDigSSIMaxFreq is set to 400. Internally, the transfer frequency is set to 200 kHz. ||If the encoder cable is very long, ENCDigSSIMaxFreq may have to be reduced. In this case, the response time of the drive is slightly reduced. The higher the transfer frequency, the lower the lag time in the control loop.||------------------------------||Prgnr: 0912.00||This parameter is only relevant for SSI encoders (singleturn and multiturn). ||The maximum possible SSI transfer frequency is encoder-specific (specified by encoder manufacturer). The value of ENCDigSSIMaxFreq and the possible SSI transfer frequencies of the encoder module are used to configure an optimum SSI transfer frequency (the encoder module supports 0.2 MHz and 1 MHz transfer frequencies).||Example: The encoder has a maximum transfer frequency of 400 kHz. ENCDigSSIMaxFreq is set to 400. Internally, the transfer frequency is set to 200 kHz. ||If the encoder cable is very long, ENCDigSSIMaxFreq may have to be reduced. In this case, the response time of the drive is slightly reduced. The higher the transfer frequency, the lower the lag time in the control loop.||||Available as of software version V01.01.||------------------------------||Einheit: kHz||Defaultwert: 200||"
"TIP"
82,6,"Prgnr: 0000.00||The maximum possible ABI frequency is encoder-specific (specified by the encoder manufacturer). The encoder module DIG supports a maximum ABI frequency of 1 MHz (this is the default and maximum value of ENCDigABIMaxFreq). An ABI frequency of 1 MHz means that there are 4000000 encoder increments in 1 second.||------------------------------||Prgnr: 0912.00||The maximum possible ABI frequency is encoder-specific (specified by the encoder manufacturer). The encoder module DIG supports a maximum ABI frequency of 1 MHz (this is the default and maximum value of ENCDigABIMaxFreq). An ABI frequency of 1 MHz means that there are 4000000 encoder increments in 1 second.||||Available as of software version V01.01.||------------------------------||Einheit: kHz||Defaultwert: 1000||"
"TIP"
82,7,"Prgnr: 0000.00||In the case of a reference movement to the index pulse, ENCDigABImaxIx contains the maximum distance within which the index pulse must be found. If no physical index pulse is found over this range, an error message is generated.||||Example: A rotary ABI encoder with one index pulse per revolution is connected. The resolution of the encoder is 8000 encoder increments per revolution (this value can be determined using parameter _Inc_Enc2Raw. _Inc_Enc2Raw and ENCDigABImaxIx have the same scaling). The maximum distance necessary for a reference movement to the index pulse is one revolution. This means that ENCDigABImaxIx should be set to 8000. Internally, a tolerance of 10% is added. This means that during a reference movement to the index pulse, an index pulse must be found within 8800 encoder increments.||------------------------------||Prgnr: 0912.00||In the case of a reference movement to the index pulse, ENCDigABImaxIx contains the maximum distance within which the index pulse must be found. (IclA NT)||15 - Hallsensors 24 Inc/Rev.  (IclA NT)||16 - Hallsensor (BLP14)||17 - Hallsensor + incremental encoder (BLP14)||Komponente :||||Ehemals Belegung wie Motorgebertyp in DEVICE.MOTTYPE,||also z.B. 500000 = SKS36||||Der Wert 8 darf nicht für einen Speziellen Encodertyp verwendet werden.
